بشرعه. وأطلق في قوله قذف مراراً فشمل ما إذا كان المقذوف واحداً أو جماعة فقذفهم بكلمة واحدة أو بكلمات، وشمل ما إذا كان في يوم أو أيام وما إذا طلبوا الحد كلهم أو بعضهم، وما إذا حضروا أو حضر أحدهم كما في الخانية وغيرها، وما إذا جلد للقذف إلا سوطاً ثم قذف آخر في المجلس فإنه يتم الأول ولا يثنى عليه للثاني للتداخل وما إذا قذف عبداً فأعتق ثم قذف آخر فأخذه الأول فضرب أربعين ثم أخذه الثاني :قالوا فإنه يتم له ثمانين لأن الأربعين وقع لهما فيبقى للباقي أربعين، ولو قذف الآخر قبل أن يأتي به فالثمانون تكون لهما جميعاً ولا يضرب ثمانين مستأنفاً لأن ما بقي تمامه حد الأحرار فجاز أن يدخل فيه الأحرار. وفي المحيط : رجل شرب الخمر فضرب بعض الحد ثم هرب ثم شرب ثانياً ضرب حداً مستقبلاً، وكذا لو ضرب الزاني بعض الحد ثم هرب وزنى بأخرى، ولو ضرب القاذف بعض الحد فهرب ثم قذف آخر ثم قدم إلى القاضي ينظر ; إن حضر المقذوف الثاني والأول جميعاً يكمل الأول ويسقط الثاني لأنه يتداخل، وإن حضر الثاني دون الأول يضرب جلداً مستقبلاً للثاني ويبطل الأول لأنه أمكن إقامة الحد للثاني لوجود دعواه ولا يمكن الإقامة للأول لعدم دعواه .اهـ. فتعين حمل ما تقدم من أنه لو جلد للقذف إلا سوطاً إلى آخره على ما إذا حضراً جميعاً، ومن أنه لو قذف جماعة يكتفى بحد واحد على ما إذا كان القذف لهم قبل أن يضرب البعض كما لا يخفى . ينبغي وشمل ما إذا قال الرجل يابن الزانيين فعليه حد واحد حيين كانا أو ميتين. وحكي أن ابن أبي ليلى سمع من يقول لرجل يابن الزانيين فحده حدين في المسجد فبلغ أبا حنيفة فقال : يا للعجب لقاضي بلدتنا أخطأ في مسألة واحدة في خمسة مواضع: الأول حده بدون طلب المقذوف. والثاني أنه لو خاصم وجب حد واحد والثالث أنه إن كان الواجب عنده حدين أن يتربص بينهما يوماً أو أكثر حتى يخف أثر الضرب الأول. والرابع ضربه في المسجد. والخامس ينبغي أن يتعرف أن والديه في الأحياء أو لا، فإن كانا حيين فالخصومة لهما وإلا فالخصومة للابن. وأفاد بقوله فحد أن الحد وقع بعد الفعل المتكرر إذ لو حد للأول ثم فعل الثاني يحد حداً آخر للثاني، سواء كان قذفاً أو زناً أو شرباً كما صرح به في القدير وغيره لكن ينبغي أن يستثنى منه ما إذا قذف رجلاً فحد له ثم عاد فقذفه ثانياً فإنه لا يحد ثانياً لأن المقصود وهو إظهار كذب القاذف ودفع العار عن المقذوف قد حصل بالأول فلا حاجة إلى الثاني صرح به الشارح الزيلعي في حد السرقة عند مسألة سرقة العين ثانياً بعد ما قطع، ولا يخفى ما فيه فإن بالحد الأول لم يظهر كذبه في إخبار مستقبل إنما ظهر فتح الكفر أو الرق غير ثابت وما هنا على ما إذا كان ثابتاً ثم رأيته لكن في الفتح والمراد قذفها بعد الإعلام بزنا كان في نصرانيتها بأن قال زنيت وأنت كافرة وكذا لو قال المعتق زنى وهو عبد زنيت وأنت عبد لا يحد كما لو قال قذفتك بالزنا وأنت مكاتبة أو أمة فلا حد عليه لأنه إنما أقر
In His legislation: He said 'slander repeatedly' includes whether the slandered is one person or a group, by one word or multiple words, in one day or many days, and whether all or some demand the hadd, and whether they are all present or only one, as in al-Khaniya and others. And if he is lashed for slander except one whip, then he slanders another in the same session, he completes the first and does not add for the second due to merging. And if he slanders a slave then the slave is freed, then he slanders another, then the first takes him and beats him forty (lashes), then the second takes him: they said he completes eighty because the forty was for both, so forty remain for the remaining. And if he slanders the other before he brings him, then the eighty is for both, and he is not flogged eighty anew because what remains is the completion of the hadd of free men, so it is permissible for free men to enter into it. In al-Muhit: A man drank wine and was given part of the hadd, then fled, then drank again: he is given a fresh hadd. Similarly, if the fornicator was given part of the hadd, then fled and committed fornication with another woman. And if the slanderer was given part of the hadd, then fled, then slandered another, then came to the judge: he considers; if the second and first slandered are both present, he completes the first and drops the second because they merge. If only the second is present, he flogs a fresh one for the second and invalidates the first, because it is possible to establish the hadd for the second due to his claim, and not possible for the first due to lack of claim. End. So it is determined that what preceded regarding 'if he is lashed for slander except one whip etc.' applies when both are present, and that 'if he slanders a group, one hadd suffices' applies when the slander of them occurred before he beats some, as is not hidden. It includes when a man says 'O son of two fornicators' — he gets one hadd whether they are alive or dead. It is narrated that Ibn Abi Layla heard someone saying to a man 'O son of two fornicators' and he gave him two hadd in the mosque. Abu Hanifa was told and said: 'O wonder! The judge of our town made a mistake in one issue in five places: First, he gave hadd without the slandered's request. Second, if he disputed, one hadd is obligatory. Third, if he thought two were obligatory, he should delay between them by a day or more so the effect of the first beating is light. Fourth, he beat him in the mosque. Fifth, he should ascertain whether his parents are alive or not; if they are alive, the claim is theirs, otherwise the claim is for the son.' And his saying 'then he hadd' indicates that the hadd occurs after repeated act; so if he hadd for the first then he does the second, he gives another hadd for the second, whether it is slander, fornication, or drinking, as stated in al-Quduri and others. But an exception should be made: if he slanders a man and is hadd for him, then returns and slanders him again, he is not hadd a second time, because the purpose — showing the slanderer's lie and removing disgrace from the slandered — has been achieved by the first, so no need for the second. This is stated by al-Zayla'i in the section on theft regarding the issue of stealing the same object again after amputation. And it is not hidden that in the first hadd his lie in future reports did not appear; it only appeared (from) the opening of disbelief or slavery not established. And what is here applies when it is established. Then I saw, but in al-Fath, what is meant is slandering her after informing of zina that was in her Christianity, by saying 'You committed zina when you were a disbeliever.' Similarly, if a freed slave says 'He committed zina when he was a slave' — 'You committed zina when you were a slave' — he is not hadd, just as if he says 'I slandered you with zina when you were a mukataba or slave girl' — there is no hadd on him because he only admitted.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Kanz al-Daqa'iq statement 'qadhf mararan' (slander repeatedly). The commentator, al-Marghinani, expands on the rulings related to multiple slanders. He explains that the phrase covers various scenarios: slandering one person or many, with one word or multiple words, over one day or several days. The key principle is that if multiple slanders occur before any punishment is inflicted, they merge (تداخل) into a single hadd. However, if some punishment has already been carried out, the remaining slanders may require completion of the original hadd or a new one depending on presence of claimants. The commentator then relates a famous incident involving Ibn Abi Layla, a judge, who erroneously imposed two hadd on a man for saying 'O son of two fornicators.' Abu Hanifa critiqued this in five points: (1) he gave hadd without the slandered person's demand, (2) even if there were a dispute, only one hadd is required, (3) if two hadd were considered necessary, they should be delayed to allow healing, (4) punishment should not be carried out in a mosque, (5) he should have checked the parents' status. The passage also discusses the repetition of the offense after punishment: if one commits the same act again after being punished, a new hadd is required, except in the case of slandering the same person again with the same accusation, because the purpose is already achieved. The exception is supported by the precedent of Abu Bakra's case. The commentator also addresses slandering non-Muslims and slaves, stating that if the slandered was a disbeliever at the time of the alleged zina, no hadd is imposed because the accusation does not imply defamation in the Islamic sense.

Key Terms
تداخل (tadakhul): Merging of multiple legal obligations into one punishment when they are of the same type and occur before any penalty is executed.
حد القذف (hadd al-qadhf): The fixed punishment for false accusation of zina: 80 lashes for a free person.
استثناء (istithna): Exception: the ruling that if the same person is slandered again after being hadd for the same accusation, no new hadd is imposed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One hadd
B) Two hadd
C) No hadd because the parents are not present
D) One hadd per parent

Key Takeaway
Multiple slanders before punishment merge into one hadd, and repeating the same slander after punishment incurs no new hadd because the purpose is already achieved.

Slandering a Slave or Non-Muslim with Zina
Ruling on slander of slaves/non-Muslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on slandering a slave or non-Muslim with zina and explain why the hadd is not applied.

Core Idea
Slandering a non-Muslim or slave with zina does not incur hadd; only ta'zir applies.

In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author discusses the limits of the fixed punishment (hadd) for slander (qadhf). While accusing a chaste Muslim of zina carries a fixed penalty of 80 lashes, the same accusation against a non-Muslim or a slave does not trigger the hadd. Understanding the rationale—that the hadd is specifically for protecting Muslim lineage and that zina can be factually committed by a non-Muslim—clarifies the scope of hudud punishments. However, such slander may still be punishable by ta'zir at the judge's discretion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and victim
Pinpoint the act: slander (qadhf) by accusing someone of zina. The victims in focus are non-Muslims and slaves.
The text specifically mentions 'mamluk' (slave) and 'kafir' (non-Muslim).
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that the hadd (80 lashes) is not imposed. Instead, the offense may be punished by ta'zir.
The author says 'لم يلزم حده' (his hadd is not necessary).
3
Explain the rationale
The reason given: because zina can be factually true for a non-Muslim (since zina is a sin in Islam but non-Muslims are not bound by Islamic rulings); thus the accusation is not automatically false. Similarly, for a slave, the hadd of qadhf is not applicable because the harm to lineage is different.
The text says 'لأن الزنا يتحقق من الكافر' (because zina is verified from the disbeliever).
4
Identify the practical consequence
Since no hadd applies, the judge may impose a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) if he deems it necessary for deterrence.
This is implicit from the placement of this ruling at the beginning of the ta'zir section.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قذف مملوكاً أو كافراً بالزنا أو مسلماً بيا فاسق يا کافر یا خبيث يا لص يا ومن الله عنه أنه قذفها في حال لو علمنا منه صريح القذف لم يلزم حده لأن الزنا يتحقق من الكافر ولذا يقام عليه الجلد حداً بخلاف الرجم على ما مر ولا يسقط الحد بالإسلام وكذا العبد. قوله: (فظهر أن المذهب إطلاق المسألة الخ) أي ظهر مما ذكره عن الظهيرية بقوله لم يحد أن المذهب إطلاق المسألة عما قيدها به في الفتح لأن كلام الظهيرية مطلق مثل كلام الزيلعي ولا يمكن أن يدعي تقييده استدلاله بالمروي عن أبي بكرة ينافيه لأن قوله أشهد أن المغيرة لزان غير مقيد بالزنا الأول ولكنه بعيد، بل الظاهر من قوله أشهد أن المراد الزنا الأول الذي عاينه منه قوله: (والفقء) أي لو فقأ عين رجل كما في النهر . قال الرملي والذي يظهر أن المراد به ذهاب البصر تأمل. فصل في التعزير تأديب دون الحد وأصله من العزر بمعنى الرد والردع ؛ كذا في المغرب وفي ضياء لأن قوله: (فالظاهر إن ما في ضياء الحلوم الخ) قال في النهر في القاموس : إنه من أسماء
Slandering a slave or a disbeliever with zina, or a Muslim with 'O sinner, O disbeliever, O wicked, O thief, O ...' — because he slandered her in a state where if we knew from him an explicit slander, his hadd would not be necessary because zina is verified from the disbeliever, therefore flogging as hadd is established on him, unlike stoning as passed, and Islam does not drop the hadd; similarly the slave. His saying: (It appears that the school is unrestricted in the issue) means it appeared from what he mentioned from al-Zahiriyyah by his saying 'he did not hadd' that the school is unrestricted regarding what was restricted in al-Fath, because the statement of al-Zahiriyyah is absolute like that of al-Zayla'i, and its restriction cannot be claimed by his inference from the narration about Abu Bakra, because his saying 'I testify that al-Mughira is a fornicator' is not restricted to the first zina, but it is distant; rather, what is apparent from his saying 'I testify' is that he means the first zina which he witnessed from him. His saying: (and the gouging) means if he gouged out a man's eye as in al-Nahr. Al-Ramli said: and what appears is that it means loss of sight, reflect. Section on Ta'zir: discipline below the hadd; its origin from 'azr meaning prevention and deterrence; as in al-Maghrib and in Diya' because his saying: (It appears that what is in Diya' al-Hulum etc.) He said in al-Nahr from al-Qamus that it is one of the names.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage covers two main topics. First, the ruling on slander (qadhf) when the victim is a slave or a non-Muslim. The key point: if someone says to a disbeliever 'you committed zina,' no hadd is imposed because zina can be factually committed by a disbeliever; the accusation is not false by default. Similarly, if a slave is slandered, no hadd applies. The same applies if the accuser says 'you committed zina when you were a slave' or 'when you were a non-Muslim.' This is because the hadd for qadhf is specifically for defaming a Muslim's reputation; slandering a non-Muslim or slave does not cause the same harm in Islamic law. However, such actions may be subject to ta'zir. Second, the passage transitions to the section on ta'zir (تعزير). The author defines ta'zir linguistically as 'prevention and deterrence' (from 'azr) and legally as 'discipline below the hadd' — i.e., punishments that are not fixed by the shari'a but are left to the discretion of the judge for offenses that do not carry a fixed hadd or kaffara. The definition is derived from al-Maghrib and other sources. The passage also includes some commentary on the term 'faqa' (gouging) mentioned in the main text.

Key Terms
قذف (qadhf): Slander, specifically false accusation of zina.
مملوك (mamluk): A slave, male or female.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because non-Muslims are not protected by Islamic law.
B) Because zina can be factually committed by a non-Muslim.
C) Because the accuser must be Muslim.
D) Because the punishment is left to the victim.

Key Takeaway
Hadd for qadhf is only for Muslim victims; slandering a non-Muslim or slave incurs no fixed hadd but may be subject to ta'zir.

Definition of Ta'zir: Discretionary Punishment
Definition of ta'zir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ta'zir linguistically and legally according to the Hanafi school and differentiate it from hadd.

Core Idea
Ta'zir is discipline below the hadd; its root means prevention and deterrence.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq marks the beginning of the section on ta'zir, a crucial concept in Islamic criminal law. The author provides both a linguistic and a legal definition, explaining that ta'zir is a punishment that is not fixed by shari'a but is left to the judge's discretion. Understanding ta'zir is essential for grasping the flexibility of Islamic jurisprudence in dealing with offenses that do not fall under the fixed hudud.

Guided Path
1
Extract the linguistic definition
The text says 'wa asluhu min al-'azr bi-ma'na al-radd wa al-rad''. So the root 'azr means prevention and deterrence.
The author cites al-Maghrib and Diya' for this etymology.
2
Extract the legal definition
The text says 'ta'dib duna al-hadd' meaning discipline below the fixed punishment. So legally, ta'zir is a discretionary punishment less severe than hadd.
This distinguishes it from hudud which have fixed penalties.
3
Relate definition to application
Since ta'zir is not fixed, the judge determines the type and severity based on the offense, the offender, and the circumstances.
Ta'zir can range from a reprimand to imprisonment or flogging, as long as it is below the minimum hadd (which is usually 40 or 80 lashes).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قذف مملوكاً أو كافراً بالزنا أو مسلماً بيا فاسق يا کافر یا خبيث يا لص يا ومن الله عنه أنه قذفها في حال لو علمنا منه صريح القذف لم يلزم حده لأن الزنا يتحقق من الكافر ولذا يقام عليه الجلد حداً بخلاف الرجم على ما مر ولا يسقط الحد بالإسلام وكذا العبد. قوله: (فظهر أن المذهب إطلاق المسألة الخ) أي ظهر مما ذكره عن الظهيرية بقوله لم يحد أن المذهب إطلاق المسألة عما قيدها به في الفتح لأن كلام الظهيرية مطلق مثل كلام الزيلعي ولا يمكن أن يدعي تقييده استدلاله بالمروي عن أبي بكرة ينافيه لأن قوله أشهد أن المغيرة لزان غير مقيد بالزنا الأول ولكنه بعيد، بل الظاهر من قوله أشهد أن المراد الزنا الأول الذي عاينه منه قوله: (والفقء) أي لو فقأ عين رجل كما في النهر . قال الرملي والذي يظهر أن المراد به ذهاب البصر تأمل. فصل في التعزير تأديب دون الحد وأصله من العزر بمعنى الرد والردع ؛ كذا في المغرب وفي ضياء لأن قوله: (فالظاهر إن ما في ضياء الحلوم الخ) قال في النهر في القاموس : إنه من أسماء
Slandering a slave or a disbeliever with zina, or a Muslim with 'O sinner, O disbeliever, O wicked, O thief, O ...' — because he slandered her in a state where if we knew from him an explicit slander, his hadd would not be necessary because zina is verified from the disbeliever, therefore flogging as hadd is established on him, unlike stoning as passed, and Islam does not drop the hadd; similarly the slave. His saying: (It appears that the school is unrestricted in the issue) means it appeared from what he mentioned from al-Zahiriyyah by his saying 'he did not hadd' that the school is unrestricted regarding what was restricted in al-Fath, because the statement of al-Zahiriyyah is absolute like that of al-Zayla'i, and its restriction cannot be claimed by his inference from the narration about Abu Bakra, because his saying 'I testify that al-Mughira is a fornicator' is not restricted to the first zina, but it is distant; rather, what is apparent from his saying 'I testify' is that he means the first zina which he witnessed from him. His saying: (and the gouging) means if he gouged out a man's eye as in al-Nahr. Al-Ramli said: and what appears is that it means loss of sight, reflect. Section on Ta'zir: discipline below the hadd; its origin from 'azr meaning prevention and deterrence; as in al-Maghrib and in Diya' because his saying: (It appears that what is in Diya' al-Hulum etc.) He said in al-Nahr from al-Qamus that it is one of the names.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage covers two main topics. First, the ruling on slander (qadhf) when the victim is a slave or a non-Muslim. The key point: if someone says to a disbeliever 'you committed zina,' no hadd is imposed because zina can be factually committed by a disbeliever; the accusation is not false by default. Similarly, if a slave is slandered, no hadd applies. The same applies if the accuser says 'you committed zina when you were a slave' or 'when you were a non-Muslim.' This is because the hadd for qadhf is specifically for defaming a Muslim's reputation; slandering a non-Muslim or slave does not cause the same harm in Islamic law. However, such actions may be subject to ta'zir. Second, the passage transitions to the section on ta'zir (تعزير). The author defines ta'zir linguistically as 'prevention and deterrence' (from 'azr) and legally as 'discipline below the hadd' — i.e., punishments that are not fixed by the shari'a but are left to the discretion of the judge for offenses that do not carry a fixed hadd or kaffara. The definition is derived from al-Maghrib and other sources. The passage also includes some commentary on the term 'faqa' (gouging) mentioned in the main text.

Key Terms
تعزير (ta'zir): A discretionary punishment less than the fixed hadd, intended to deter and reform the offender.
عزر ('azr): Linguistic root meaning prevention and deterrence, from which ta'zir is derived.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the linguistic origin of ta'zir according to the passage?
A) From 'azr meaning to honor.
B) From 'azr meaning prevention and deterrence.
C) From tazir meaning to support.
D) From 'uzr meaning excuse.

Key Takeaway
Ta'zir is a discretionary punishment below the hadd, linguistically rooted in 'azr (prevention), giving judges flexibility to deter and reform.

Repeating Qadhf After Hadd
Ruling on repeating qadhf after hadd execution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi ruling on repeating qadhf after hadd and evaluate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Fath al-Qadir and al-Zahiriyyah.

Core Idea
After hadd for qadhf, no second hadd is ever imposed for any accusation against the same person.

This passage addresses a subtle intra-Hanafi disagreement: if someone is punished for falsely accusing another of zina, and then repeats the accusation, does he receive a second hadd? The text presents two positions within the school and resolves the issue by citing a Companion consensus. Understanding this ruling clarifies the limits of hadd punishments and the principle of finality after execution.

Guided Path
1
Parse the two positions
Identify the view from Fath al-Qadir (distinguishes same vs new accusation) and from al-Zahiriyyah (absolute no second hadd).
Fath al-Qadir: same accusation no new hadd, new accusation of a different act triggers new hadd. al-Zahiriyyah: absolute no new hadd for any repetition.
2
Locate the dalil naqli
The story of Abu Bakrah: he was punished by 'Umar, then repeated the accusation; 'Umar wanted to punish again but 'Ali prevented him, and 'Umar retracted, creating consensus.
This incident is the basis for the absolute view.
3
Understand the legal principle
Once hadd is executed, the matter is concluded; repeating the same accusation does not restart the process.
The hadd is considered expiation and final.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Fath al-Qadir, a new accusation of a different act of zina triggers a new hadd; under the absolute view, never.
Practical consequence of the difference.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The author sides with al-Zahiriyyah, so the relied-upon ruling is absolute: no second hadd.
Mufta bihi: no second hadd for any repeated qadhf against the same person.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قذف مملوكاً أو كافراً بالزنا أو مسلماً بيا فاسق يا کافر یا خبيث يا لص يا ومن الله عنه كذبه فيما أخبر به ماضياً قبل الحد ولهذا ذكر المحقق في فتح القدير عند تلك المسألة، وصار كما لو قذف شخصاً فحد به ثم قذفه بعين ذلك الزنا بأن قال أنا باق على نسبتي إليه الزنا الذي نسبته إليه لا يحد ثانياً فكذا هذا، أما إذا قذفه بزنا آخر حد به ا هـ. لكن في الظهيرية : ومن قذف إنساناً فحد ثم قذفه ثانياً لم يحد. والأصل فيه ما روي أن أبا بكرة لما شهد على المغيرة بالزنا وجلده عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه لقصور العدد بالشهادة كان يقول بعد ذلك في المحافل : أشهد أن المغيرة لزان فأراد عمر رضي الله عنه أن يحده ثانياً فمنعه علي فرجع إلى قوله وصارت المسألة إجماعاً اهـ .بلفظه فظهر أن المذهب إطلاق المسألة كما ذكره الزيلعي
If he accuses a slave or a disbeliever of zina, or a Muslim by saying 'O sinner, O disbeliever, O wicked, O thief, O...' and he lies in what he informed about past [zina] before the hadd, and for this reason the investigator mentioned in Fath al-Qadir at that issue: It is as if he accused a person and was hadded for it, then he accused him of that same zina by saying 'I remain upon my attribution to him of the zina which I attributed to him' – he is not hadded a second time. So is this case. But if he accused him of another zina, he is hadded for it. However, in al-Zahiriyyah: Whoever accuses a person and is hadded, then accuses him a second time, he is not hadded. The basis for this is what was narrated: that Abu Bakrah testified against al-Mughirah for zina, and 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him, flogged him due to insufficient witnesses, [but] he used to say afterwards in gatherings: 'I testify that al-Mughirah is a fornicator.' So 'Umar wanted to hadd him a second time, but 'Ali prevented him, so he retracted and the issue became consensus. The end. By his wording, it became apparent that the madhhab is the absolute ruling as al-Zayla'i mentioned.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on repeating the accusation of zina (qadhf) after the hadd punishment has already been executed. The author presents two views: one from Fath al-Qadir that if the same accusation is repeated, no new hadd is required, but if a different accusation of zina is made, a new hadd is required; and another from al-Zahiriyyah that absolutely no second hadd is imposed regardless. The author supports the second view by citing the incident of Abu Bakrah, who was punished by 'Umar for qadhf against al-Mughirah, and later repeated the accusation in public. 'Umar wanted to punish him again, but 'Ali prevented him, and 'Umar accepted his opinion, leading to consensus. Thus, the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that repeating the same qadhf does not incur a second hadd.

Key Terms
قذف (qadhf): Falsely accusing a chaste person of zina (unlawful sexual intercourse).
حد (hadd): A fixed, prescribed punishment for certain offenses (e.g., zina, qadhf, theft) that cannot be altered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on someone who was hadded for qadhf and then repeats the exact same accusation?
A) He must be hadded again for repeating the accusation.
B) He is not hadded again for that accusation.
C) He is hadded only if he uses different words.
D) He should be imprisoned instead.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, after a hadd for qadhf is executed, the same accusation cannot trigger a second hadd, based on Companion consensus.

Order of Execution When Multiple Hudud Accumulate
Ruling on sequence of hadd punishments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of executing multiple hudud on one person and explain the basis in the Companions' ijtihad.

Core Idea
When multiple hudud combine, the fixed order is: qisas, qadhf, then choose between theft and zina, drinking last.

The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq did not address the case of multiple different hudud on one person. The text from al-Muhit fills this gap by prescribing a specific sequence based on the ijtihad of the Companions. This lesson unpacks that order and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
When multiple different hudud accumulate on one person, they are not executed simultaneously; a specific order must be followed.
The text assumes all punishments are legally due and physically possible to execute.
2
Locate the proof
The order is established by the ijtihad of the Companions (ra), as cited from al-Muhit. The phrase 'li thubutihi bi al-ijtihad min al-sahabah' indicates the authority.
This is a form of ijma' (consensus) of the Companions, considered a strong source in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the reasoning
The order prioritizes qisas (a personal right mixed with divine right) first, then proceeds to hadd punishments. The judge is given discretion after the first two fixed punishments.
Qisas is given priority because it involves a victim's right, which must be fulfilled before purely divine rights.
4
Note the exception for muhsan
If the person is muhsan, after qisas and qadhf, stoning (rajm) is executed and all other punishments (theft, drinking) are dropped.
This is because stoning is the ultimate punishment for a muhsan, satisfying all other hadd claims.
5
Recognize the practical application
The judge must wait for the convict to recover from each punishment before executing the next (e.g., after qisas, wait for healing before qadhf).
The text uses 'fadha yabra' (then when he recovers) to indicate the physical capacity requirement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يذكر المصنف التداخل في حد السرقة، ولا شك فيه لأنه حق الله تعالى. ولم يذكر أيضاً ما إذا اجتمعت عليه الحدود المختلفة كيف يفعل قال في المحيط : وإذا اجتمع حدان وقدر على درء أحدهما ،درأه، وإن كانت من أجناس مختلفة بأن اجتمع حد الزنا والسرقة والشرب والقذف والفقء بدأ بالفقء، فإذا برأ حد للقذف، فإذا برأ إن شاء بدأ بالقطع وإن شاء بدأ بحد الزنا وحد الشرب آخرها لثبوته بالاجتهاد من الصحابة رضي الله عنهم، وإن كان محصناً يبدأ بالفقء ثم بحد القذف ثم بالرجم ويلغى غيرها اهـ
And the author (of Kanz al-Daqa'iq) did not mention interlock in the hadd of theft, and there is no doubt about it because it is the right of Allah. And he also did not mention when different hudud are combined on a person, what should be done. He said in al-Muhit: When two hadd punishments combine and it is possible to repel one, he repels it. And if they are of different types, such as the hadd of zina, theft, drinking, qadhf, and blinding, he starts with blinding. Then when he recovers, he executes the hadd of qadhf. Then when he recovers, if he wishes, he starts with amputation, and if he wishes, he starts with the hadd of zina, and the hadd of drinking is last, because this is established by the ijtihad of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. And if he is muhsan, he starts with blinding, then the hadd of qadhf, then stoning, and other punishments are dropped. End.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario not covered by the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq: when a person is liable for multiple different hudud (e.g., zina, theft, drinking, qadhf, and qisas for blinding). The order is: first execute qisas (eye-for-eye), then when healed, execute hadd for qadhf, then the judge may choose to start with amputation for theft or hadd for zina, with hadd for drinking last. For a muhsan (married person), after qisas and qadhf, he is stoned to death (rajm), and the other punishments are dropped. This order is based on the ijtihad of the Companions.

Key Terms
فقء (faq'): Blinding or putting out an eye; here it refers to qisas for causing loss of eyesight.
محصن (muhsan): A married, free, adult Muslim who has had valid consummation; liable for rajm if guilty of zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In what order are different hudud executed when they accumulate on a person who is not muhsan?
A) Qadhf, then zina, then drinking, then theft, then qisas.
B) Qisas, then qadhf, then judge chooses between theft and zina, then drinking.
C) The judge chooses any order he prefers.
D) All hudud are executed simultaneously.

Key Takeaway
When multiple hudud accumulate, the Hanafi school prescribes a fixed order: qisas first, then qadhf, then a choice between amputation and zina, with drinking last; for muhsan, stoning replaces all after qisas and qadhf.

Prohibition of Executing Hadd in the Mosque
Ruling that hadd, qisas, and ta'zir are prohibited in the mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on executing hudud, qisas, and ta'zir in the mosque and identify the proper procedure for a judge witnessing such punishments.

Core Idea
No hadd, qisas, or ta'zir may be executed inside a mosque, upholding its sanctity.

This brief but important ruling from the Hanafi school establishes that the mosque, as a place of worship and peace, must not be used for the execution of punishments. The text presents a clear prohibition and provides prophetic precedents showing the correct alternative: the judge either leaves the mosque or appoints a trustworthy deputy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited acts
The text prohibits three types of punishments: hadd (fixed penalties), qisas (retaliation), and ta'zir (discretionary punishment). Recognize each term and its scope.
Hadd offenses include theft, zina, etc.; qisas applies to homicide and bodily harm; ta'zir covers other offenses.
2
State the ruling and its basis
The ruling is that none of these punishments may be established inside the mosque. The basis is the sanctity of the mosque and the prophetic example.
The mosque is a place of worship, not punishment.
3
Recall the prophetic precedents
The Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) demonstrated two options for the judge: either exit the mosque (as with al-Ghamidiyyah) or send a trustworthy person (amin) to execute elsewhere (as with Ma'iz).
These examples show flexibility but emphasize leaving the mosque.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If a judge wishes to witness punishment, he must not stay in the mosque; he must move outside or delegate.
The prohibition is on the location, not on the judge's presence per se.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا : ولا يقام حد في المسجد ولا قود ولا تعزير ولكن القاضي إذا أراد أن يقام بحضرته يخرج من المسجد كما فعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بالغامدية أو يبعث أميناً كما فعل عليه الصلاة والسلام في ماعز رضي الله عنه
They said: No hadd, no qisas, and no ta'zir should be established in the mosque. But if the judge wants it to be established in his presence, he should exit the mosque, as the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, did with al-Ghamidiyyah, or he should send a trustworthy person, as he, peace and blessings be upon him, did with Ma'iz, may Allah be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This brief ruling states that no hadd, qisas, or ta'zir punishment should be enforced inside a mosque. Instead, if the judge wants it executed in his presence, he should leave the mosque, as the Prophet did with al-Ghamidiyyah, or send a trustworthy person, as he did with Ma'iz. This is to maintain the sanctity of the mosque.

Key Terms
قود (qisas): Retaliatory punishment for intentional homicide or bodily harm.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd or atonement.
حد (hadd): Fixed punishment prescribed by Islamic law for specific offenses (e.g., theft, zina).
أمين (amin): A trustworthy person appointed by the judge to oversee the execution of punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a judge do if he wishes to witness the execution of a hadd punishment?
A) He should remain inside the mosque and observe from a distance.
B) He should exit the mosque or send a trustworthy person.
C) He should postpone the execution until he can leave the mosque.
D) He can allow the execution in the mosque if it is a ta'zir punishment.

Key Takeaway
Hadd, qisas, and ta'zir punishments must never be executed inside a mosque; the judge must either leave or send a deputy.

Definition and Types of Ta'zir (التعزير: تعريفه وأنواعه)
Definition and categorization of ta'zir punishment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ta'zir, distinguish its linguistic and technical meanings, list the permissible methods of ta'zir according to the Hanafi school, and state the relied-upon position on confiscation of wealth.

Core Idea
Ta'zir is discretionary punishment below hadd, not limited to beating; taking wealth is not allowed in the Hanafi school.

This lesson from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defines ta'zir and explores its various forms. You will learn that while ta'zir can include several types of punishment, not all methods are universally accepted. The Hanafi school's position on confiscating wealth as ta'zir is clarified, along with the classification of punishments based on the offender's social status.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish linguistic vs. technical definition
Note that linguistically ta'zir means 'to repel' or 'to glorify', but technically it is a disciplinary punishment below the fixed hadd.
The Quranic usage (48:9) 'tu'azziruhu' illustrates the linguistic sense of glorification, not the legal term.
2
Identify the methods of ta'zir
List the forms mentioned: beating, slapping, ear-pulling, harsh words, a frown, imprisonment, and notification (i'lam).
The author emphasises that the shari'a meaning is not restricted to beating.
3
Analyse the dispute on ta'zir by taking wealth
Recognise that some narrations from Abu Yusuf allow it, but the relied-upon madhhab position prohibits it; the wealth is not to be taken for the judge or treasury.
The text concludes: 'al-madhhab 'adam al-ta'zir bi akhdh al-mal' – the school does not allow it.
4
Understand the classification by status
Note how ta'zir severity varies: mere notification for the elite (scholars, Alids); additional measures for the middle class (princes, landowners); and more severe for the lowly (including beating).
This classification is found in al-Shafi.
5
Determine mufta bihi for each type
Based on the text, identify which forms are permitted (e.g., beating, imprisonment, notification) and which are not (e.g., slapping by some views, confiscation of wealth).
The judge must exercise ijtihad within these boundaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في التعزير تأديب دون الحد وأصله من العزر بمعنى الرد والردع؛ كذا في المغرب وفي ضياء الحلوم هو ضرب دون الحد للتأديب والتعزير التعظيم والنصر قال تعالى وتعزروه [الفتح : 9] اهـ فالظاهر أن ما في ضياء الحلوم معناه اللغوي وما في المغرب معناه الشرعي فإنه شرعاً لا يختص بالضرب بل قد يكون به وقد يكون بالصفع وبفرك الأذن، وقد يكون بالكلام العنيف، وقد يكون بنظر القاضي إليه بوجه عبوس وذكر أبو اليسر والسرخسي لا يباح التعزير بالصفع لأنه من أعلى ما يكون من الاستخفاف فيصان عنه أهل الغفلة؛ كذا في المجتبى. وفي ضياء الحلوم الصفع الضرب على القفا. ولم يذكر محمد التعزير بأخذ المال وقد قيل : روي عن أبي يوسف أن التعزير من السلطان بأخذ المال جائز ؛ كذا في الظهيرية . وفي الخلاصة : سمعت عن ثقة أن التعزير بأخذ المال إن رأى القاضي ذلك أو الوالي جاز، ومن جملة ذلك رجل لا يحضر الجماعة يجوز تعزيره بأخذ المال اهـ. وأفاد في البزازية أن معنى التعزير بأخذ المال على القول به إمساك شيء من ماله عند مدة لينزجر ثم يعيده الحاكم إليه لا أن يأخذه الحاكم لنفسه أو لبيت المال كما يتوهمه الظلمة إذ لا يجوز لأحد من المسلمين أخذ مال أحد بغير سبب شرعي. وفي المجتبى : لم يذكر كيفية الأخذ وأرى أن يأخذها فيمسكها فإن أيس من توبته يصرفها إلى ما يرى. وفي شرح الآثار التعزير بالمال كان في ابتداء الإسلام ثم نسخ .اهـ. والحاصل أن المذهب عدم التعزير بأخذ المال، وأما التعزير بالشتم فلم أره إلا في المجتبى قال : وفي شرح أبي اليسر : التعزير بالشتم مشروع ولكن بعد أن لا يكون السرخسي بأنه ليس في التعزير شيء مقدر بل هو مفوض إلى رأي القاضي الأن المقصود منه الزجر وأحوال الناس مختلفة فيه. وفي الشافي: التعزير على مراتب : أشراف الأشراف وهم العلماء والعلوية بالإعلام وهو أن يقول له القاضي إنك تفعل كذا وكذا فينزجر به. وتعزير الأشراف وهم الأمراء والدهاقين بالإعلام والجر إلى باب القاضي والخصومة. وتعزير الأوساط وهم السوقة بالجر والحبس. وتعزير الأخسة بهذا كله وبالضرب
Chapter on Ta'zir: It is a discipline below the hadd. Its origin is from 'azr meaning repelling and preventing. Thus in al-Mughrib. And in Diya' al-Huloom, it is beating below the hadd for discipline. And ta'zir means glorification and victory. Allah said: 'And you glorify Him' (48:9). So it appears that what is in Diya' al-Huloom is its linguistic meaning, and what is in al-Mughrib is its legal meaning. For according to shari'a, it is not restricted to beating, but may be with beating, with slapping, with rubbing the ear, with harsh words, and with the judge looking at him with a frowning face. Abu al-Yusr and al-Sarakhsi mentioned that ta'zir by slapping is not permissible because it is the highest form of contempt, so it should be avoided for the heedless; thus in al-Mujtaba. And in Diya' al-Huloom, slapping is hitting on the back of the neck. And Muhammad did not mention ta'zir by taking wealth. And it was said: It was narrated from Abu Yusuf that ta'zir by the ruler taking wealth is permissible; thus in al-Zahiriyyah. And in al-Khulasah: I heard from a reliable person that ta'zir by taking wealth is permissible if the judge or governor deems it, and from that is a man who does not attend the congregation; his ta'zir by taking wealth is permissible. End. And it was stated in al-Bazzaziyyah that the meaning of ta'zir by taking wealth, according to those who say it, is to detain something from his wealth for a period so that he desists, then the ruler returns it to him, not that the ruler takes it for himself or for the treasury as the oppressors imagine, for it is not permissible for any Muslim to take the wealth of another without a legitimate legal reason. And in al-Mujtaba: He did not mention the method of taking; I think he should take it and hold it; if he despairs of his repentance, he should spend it as he sees fit. And in Sharh al-Athar: Ta'zir by wealth was in the beginning of Islam, then abrogated. The summary: The madhhab is that there is no ta'zir by taking wealth. As for ta'zir by verbal abuse, I have not seen it except in al-Mujtaba, where it says: And in Sharh Abi al-Yusr: Ta'zir by verbal abuse is legislated, but only after... And al-Sarakhsi stated that there is nothing measured in ta'zir; rather it is left to the opinion of the judge because the intention is deterrence and the conditions of people differ. And in al-Shafi: Ta'zir is of ranks: The highest of the high, i.e., scholars and Alids, by notification (i'lam) – the judge says to him 'You do such and such' and he desists. And ta'zir of the high, i.e., princes and landowners, by notification and dragging to the judge's door and litigation. And ta'zir of the middle, i.e., ordinary people, by dragging and imprisonment. And ta'zir of the lowly is by all of these and by beating.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage defines ta'zir linguistically and technically. Linguistically, it means 'repelling' or 'preventing'. Technically, it is a disciplinary punishment below the prescribed hadd. The author discusses various methods: beating, slapping, ear-pulling, harsh words, or even a stern look. There is disagreement on slapping, with some scholars prohibiting it as too degrading. Regarding confiscation of wealth, some narrate from Abu Yusuf that it is permissible, but the relied-upon position of the madhhab is that it is not allowed. The purpose is deterrence, and the punishment is left to the judge's discretion, though beating cannot exceed 39 lashes (as mentioned later). Finally, ta'zir is categorized according to the social status of the offender: for the elite (scholars and descendants of the Prophet), mere notification suffices; for the common people, more severe measures like imprisonment and beating may be used.

Key Terms
تعزير (ta'zir): A discretionary punishment for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd or kaffarah, left to the judge's discretion.
صفع (saf'): Slapping or hitting on the back of the neck; considered a severe form of humiliation.
إعلام (i'lam): Notification; the judge simply informs the offender of his wrongdoing, which serves as deterrence for high-status individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, which of the following is NOT a valid form of ta'zir?
A) Notification (i'lam)
B) Beating (darb)
C) Taking wealth (akhdh al-mal)
D) Imprisonment (habs)

Key Takeaway
Ta'zir is a discretionary punishment below hadd; its forms are left to the judge but must not include confiscation of wealth, and severity varies with the offender's social status.

Definition and Forms of Ta'zir in Hanafi Fiqh
Definition and enumeration of ta'zir forms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal definition of ta'zir and identify its permissible forms according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Ta'zir is any discretionary punishment less than hadd, including words, looks, or beating—not limited to the whip.

Ta'zir is a cornerstone of Islamic penal policy: it allows the judge to respond to crimes that do not have a fixed hadd punishment. But what exactly counts as ta'zir? In this passage, the commentator defines ta'zir both linguistically and legally, then lists the diverse forms it can take—from a stern glance to imprisonment. Understanding this scope is essential before exploring the detailed rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic and legal meanings
Read the opening line: 'al-ta'zir huwa darbun duna al-hadd li al-ta'dib' and then the citation of 48:9. Note that linguistically it means 'magnification' while legally it is 'discipline via punishment below hadd'.
The verse 'wa tu'azziruhu' gives the root meaning of support/honor, but the legal term has narrowed.
2
List the permissible forms of ta'zir
The commentator enumerates: beating, slapping, rubbing the ear, harsh speech, and even the judge's frowning look. Note the disagreement on slapping (some prohibit as too degrading).
Slapping is mentioned as prohibited by Abu al-Yusr and al-Sarakhsi because it is 'the most severe belittlement'.
3
Understand the principle of delegation
Al-Sarakhsi states: 'laysa fi al-ta'zir shay' muqaddar' – nothing is fixed; it is delegated to the judge's ijtihad based on the crime and the offender's condition.
This is a key principle: the judge has wide discretion within the bounds of not reaching hadd.
4
Note the physical maximum
Although no fixed amount, if beating is chosen, it cannot exceed 39 lashes (as will come later in Hidayah). This distinguishes it from hadd (which is 40 or 80/100).
This maximum is a boundary to keep ta'zir below the least hadd.

Source Text

والتعزير هو ضرب دون الحد للتأديب والتعزير التعظيم والنصر قال تعالى وتعزروه [ الفتح : 9 ] فالظاهر أن ما في ضياء الحلوم معناه اللغوي وما في المغرب معناه الشرعي فإنه شرعاً لا يختص بالضرب بل قد يكون به وقد يكون بالصفع وبفرك الأذن، وقد يكون بالكلام العنيف، وقد يكون بنظر القاضي إليه بوجه عبوس وذكر أبو اليسر والسرخسي لا يباح التعزير بالصفع لأنه من أعلى ما يكون من الاستخفاف فيصان عنه أهل الغفلة؛ كذا في المجتبى. وفي ضياء الحلوم الصفع الضرب على القفا. ولم يذكر محمد التعزير بأخذ المال وقد قيل : روي عن أبي يوسف أن التعزير من السلطان بأخذ المال جائز؛ كذا في الظهيرية. وفي الخلاصة : سمعت عن ثقة أن التعزير بأخذ المال إن رأى القاضي ذلك أو الوالي جاز، ومن جملة ذلك رجل لا يحضر الجماعة يجوز تعزيره بأخذ المال. وأفاد في البزازية أن معنى التعزير بأخذ المال على القول به إمساك شيء من ماله عند مدة لينزجر ثم يعيده الحاكم إليه لا أن يأخذه الحاكم لنفسه أو لبيت المال كما يتوهمه الظلمة إذ لا يجوز لأحد من المسلمين أخذ مال أحد بغير سبب شرعي. وفي المجتبى : لم يذكر كيفية الأخذ وأرى أن يأخذها فيمسكها فإن أيس من توبته يصرفها إلى ما يرى. وفي شرح الآثار التعزير بالمال كان في ابتداء الإسلام ثم نسخ. والحاصل أن المذهب عدم التعزير بأخذ المال، وأما التعزير بالشتم فلم أره إلا في المجتبى قال : وفي شرح أبي اليسر : التعزير بالشتم مشروع ولكن بعد أن لا يكون السرخسي بأنه ليس في التعزير شيء مقدر بل هو مفوض إلى رأي القاضي لأن المقصود منه الزجر وأحوال الناس مختلفة فيه. وفي الشافي: التعزير على مراتب : أشراف الأشراف وهم العلماء والعلوية بالإعلام وهو أن يقول له القاضي إنك تفعل كذا وكذا فينزجر به. وتعزير الأشراف وهم الأمراء والدهاقين بالإعلام والجر إلى باب القاضي والخصومة. وتعزير الأوساط وهم السوقة بالجر والحبس. وتعزير الأخسة بهذا كله وبالضرب. قوله : (وصرح السرخسي بأنه ليس في التعزير شيء مقدر) أي في أنواعه فإنه يكون بالضرب وغيره أما إن اقتضى رأيه الضرب فلا يزيد على تسعة وثلاثين كما يأتي. قوله : (وأحوال الناس فيه مختلفة فمنهم من ينزجر بالنصيحة، ومنهم باللطمة ومنهم من يحتاج إلى الضرب ومنهم من يحتاج إلى الحبس؛ كذا في الفتح. قوله : (وظاهره كان أنه ليس مفوضاً) قال في النهر : وينبغي أن لا يكون ما في الشافي على إطلاقه فإن من أشراف الأشراف لو ضرب غيره فأدماه لا يكتفي بتعزيره بقول القاضي ما مر إذ لا ينزجر بذلك. وقد رأيت بعض القضاة من الإخوان من أدبه بالضرب وأرى أنه صواب. أقول : يمكن أن يكون ما في الشافي بياناً لما تضمنه القول الأول . قال الزيلعي : ثم هو قد يكون بالحبس وقد يكون بالصفع وبتعريك الأذن وقد يكون بالكلام العنيف أو بالضرب، وقد يكون بنظر القاضي إليه بوجه عبوس وليس فيه شيء مقدر وإنما هو مفوض إلى رأي الإمام على ما يقتضي جنايتهم فإن العقوبة فيه تختلف باختلاف الجناية فينبغي أن يبلغ غاية التعزير في الكبيرة كما إذا أصاب من الأجنبية كل محرم سوى الجماع أو جمع السارق المتاع في الدار ولم يخرجه وكذا ينظر في أحوالهم فإن من الناس من ينزجر باليسير ومنهم من لا ينزجر إلا بالكثير. وذكر في النهاية التعزير على مراتب الخ فقوله «وذكر في النهاية الخ» يصلح بياناً لقوله وكذا ينظر في أحوالهم فصار حاصل القول بالتفويض إلى رأي الإمام أن ينظر إلى الجناية وإلى حال الجاني، فإذا كانت الجناية صغيرة والجاني ذا مروءة ممن ينزجر بمجرد الإعلام لا يزاد عليه بخلاف ما إذا كانت جنايته كبيرة كاللواطة أو شرب الخمر فإن هذا لا يصدر من ذي مروءة، وإن كان هو من الأشراف فلا ينبغي أن يقال إنه يكفي فيه مجرد الإعلام. وما في الشافي والنهاية لا ينافي ذلك لأن نحو العلماء والعلوية يراد بهم من جنايته صغيرة صدرت منه على وجه الزلة والندور ولذا قال في الخانية وغيرها لو كان ذا مروءة أول ما فعل يوعظ استحساناً ولا يعزر. وقال الناطفي : إذا تكرر منه يضرب التعزير فإن هذا ظاهر في أن تكرار ذلك منه يخرجه عن كونه ذا مروءة فكذا ما كان معصية شنيعة لا تصدر عادة من ذي مروءة والمراد كما في الفتح بالمروءة الدين والصلاح. قوله : (فقد أفاد الفرق الخ) قال في النهر : لا نسلم أن ما عن الهنداوني نص في الأجنبية لم لا يجوز أن يكون المعنى بامرأة له وخصها لتعم الأجنبية بالأولى ويدل على ذلك ما في حدود البزازية من وجد مع امرأته رجلاً إن كان ينزجر بالصياح وبما دون السلاح لا يحل قتله وإن كان لا ينزجر إلا بالقتل حل قتله، وإن طاوعته حل قتلها أيضاً، وهذا نص على أن التعزير والقتل يليه غير المحتسب. وبهذا يندفع التدافع بين كلامي
Ta'zir is beating less than the prescribed punishment for discipline and ta'zir meaning magnification and support. Allah said: 'And you honor him' [48:9]. So it appears that what is in Diya' al-Huloom is its linguistic meaning and what is in al-Maghrib is its legal meaning, for in law it is not limited to beating but may be through beating, slapping, rubbing the ear, harsh speech, or the judge looking at him with a frowning face. Abu al-Yusr and al-Sarakhsi mentioned that ta'zir by slapping is not permissible because it is the most severe belittlement, so the heedless should be protected from it; as in al-Mujtaba. In Diya' al-Huloom: slapping is hitting the back of the neck. Muhammad did not mention ta'zir by taking property, and it was said: it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that ta'zir by the ruler by taking property is permissible; as in al-Zahiriyya. In al-Khulasa: I heard from a reliable source that ta'zir by taking property if the judge or governor deems it is permissible, and among that is a man who does not attend the congregation; it is permissible to discipline him by taking his property. In al-Bazzaziyya it states that the meaning of ta'zir by taking property according to that view is that the judge detains some of his property for a period so that he will desist, then returns it to him, not that the judge takes it for himself or for the treasury as the oppressors imagine, for it is not permissible for any Muslim to take anyone's property without a legal cause. In al-Mujtaba: He did not mention the method of taking, and I think that he takes it and detains it; if he despairs of his repentance, he spends it as he sees fit. In Sharh al-Athar: Ta'zir by property existed in early Islam then was abrogated. The conclusion is that the school is that ta'zir by taking property is not allowed. As for ta'zir by verbal abuse, I have not seen it except in al-Mujtaba: In Sharh Abi al-Yusr: ta'zir by verbal abuse is legislated, but not that al-Sarakhsi stated that ta'zir has no fixed measure but is delegated to the judge's opinion because the purpose is deterrence and people's conditions differ. In al-Shafi: Ta'zir is in levels: the most noble of nobles are scholars and Alawis: by informing, which is the judge saying to him 'you do such and such' and he desists. Ta'zir of nobles (commanders and officials) is by informing and dragging to the judge's court and litigation. Ta'zir of middle class (commoners) is by dragging and imprisonment. Ta'zir of the lowly is all of that and beating. 'And al-Sarakhsi stated that ta'zir has no fixed measure' meaning its types, for it is by beating or otherwise; if his opinion requires beating, he does not exceed thirty-nine as will come. 'And people's conditions differ in it, so some are deterred by advice, some by a slap, some need beating, some need imprisonment'; as in al-Fath. 'And the apparent meaning is that it is not delegated' – in al-Nahr: It should not be that what is in al-Shafi is absolute, for if a most noble person beats another and draws blood, he will not be satisfied by the judge's mere words as he won't be deterred. I have seen some judge brothers disciplining by beating and I think it is correct. I say: It is possible that what is in al-Shafi is an explanation of what the first statement includes. Al-Zayla'i said: Then it may be by imprisonment, by slapping, rubbing the ear, harsh speech, beating, or the judge looking with a frowning face; there is no fixed measure; it is delegated to the judge's opinion according to what their crime requires, for punishment differs with the crime; so he should make the extent of ta'zir reach its maximum for major sins such as touching a non-mahram woman in any unlawful way except intercourse, or the thief gathering goods in the house without taking them out; and he should also consider their conditions, for some are deterred by little and some only by much. And in al-Nihaya, ta'zir is in levels, so his statement 'and in al-Nihaya ta'zir is in levels' may serve as an explanation of his statement 'and he should also consider their conditions', so the result of the delegation to the judge's opinion is that he considers the crime and the criminal's condition. If the crime is minor and the criminal is a man of good character who is deterred by mere notice, no more is added, unlike if his crime is major like sodomy or drinking wine, for such is not done by a man of good character, even if he is of the nobles; it should not be said that mere notice suffices for him. What is in al-Shafi and al-Nihaya does not contradict that because 'scholars and Alawis' refers to someone whose crime is minor and occurs as a slip; this is why al-Khaniya and others said: if he is a man of good character the first time, he is admonished by way of istihsan and not punished. Al-Natafi said: if it recurs, he receives ta'zir by beating, for this indicates that repetition removes him from being of good character; likewise, if the sin is heinous and not normally done by a man of good character. The meaning of 'good character' as in al-Fath is religion and righteousness. 'He thus established the distinction' – in al-Nahr: We do not accept that the statement of al-Hindwani is explicit about a foreign woman; rather it may mean his own woman and it is specified to include a foreign woman a fortiori; evidence for that is in Hudud al-Bazzaziyya: one who finds a man with his wife, if he is deterred by shouting and by less than a weapon, killing is not permissible; if he is not deterred except by killing, killing is permissible; and if she consents, killing her is also permissible. This is explicit that ta'zir and killing are for other than the muhtasib. By this the contradiction between the two statements is resolved.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the definition and application of ta'zir (discretionary punishment). The author opens by defining ta'zir linguistically and legally, citing the Qur'anic verse 'wa tu'azziruhu' (48:9) which uses the root in the sense of glorification and support. He clarifies that in legal terminology, ta'zir is not restricted to beating but includes various forms: slapping, rubbing the ear, harsh speech, or even the judge's stern look. He then discusses a difference among Hanafi scholars: Abu al-Yusr and al-Sarakhsi forbid ta'zir by slapping because it is considered extreme humiliation, while others allow it. The more significant ikhtilaf is about ta'zir by taking property: Imam Muhammad did not mention it, but a narration from Abu Yusuf permits the ruler to take property as ta'zir. Al-Khulasa reports that some authorities allow it if the judge deems it, giving the example of a man neglecting congregational prayer. However, al-Bazzaziyya clarifies that the property is merely detained and returned upon desistance, not taken permanently. The author concludes that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that ta'zir by taking property is not allowed, as it was abrogated (see Sharh al-Athar). He notes that ta'zir by verbal reprimand is mentioned only in al-Mujtaba as legislated. The passage then emphasizes that ta'zir has no fixed measure; it is delegated to the judge's discretion (tafwid ila ra'y al-qadi), considering the nature of the crime and the criminal's status. Al-Shafi (a Hanafi source, not Imam al-Shafi'i) categorizes people into four ranks with escalating methods: the most noble (scholars and Alawis) are only informed, nobles (officials) are summoned and litigated, middle class are imprisoned, and lowly are beaten. However, the commentator al-Zayla'i and the author note that this classification is not absolute; if a noble commits a major crime like killing or sodomy, mere notice is insufficient. The judge must look at the crime magnitude and the offender's character (muru'a). The passage also addresses the controversial issue of killing a man found with one's wife: al-Hindwani allows killing if the offender cannot be deterred otherwise, and even the wife if she consented. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq reconciles apparent contradictions by arguing that this applies even if the woman is a foreigner, as per al-Bazzaziyya, and that this is a case of self-defense or honor, not within the muhtasib's authority.

Key Terms
التعزير (al-ta'zir): Punishment less than the prescribed hadd, determined at the judge's discretion for tarbiyya (discipline).
المروءة (al-muru'a): Good character and sense of honor; a criterion for reducing ta'zir of a first-time minor offender.
الإعلام (al-i'lam): The judge informing the offender of his wrongdoing as a form of ta'zir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the maximum number of lashes allowed in ta'zir?
A) 9 lashes
B) 39 lashes
C) 79 lashes
D) No maximum

Key Takeaway
Ta'zir is a flexible, discretionary punishment below hadd, encompassing diverse forms from verbal admonition to physical beating, with no fixed measure but capped at 39 lashes if beating is chosen.

Killing a Found Adulterer: Conditions and Reconciliation
Fatawa on permissibility of killing a found adulterer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing a found adulterer and apply the condition of deterrence to different relationships.

Core Idea
Killing a found adulterer is permissible only when necessary; the condition varies by relationship: stricter for unrelated, absolute for wife/mahram.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq reconciles two Hanafi fatwa sources on a sensitive issue: whether a man may kill someone he catches in zina. Al-Hinduwani conditioned killing on inability to deter; al-Munya allowed it absolutely for wife/mahram. The commentator harmonizes them, establishing a clear distinction between unrelated women and close relatives. You will learn the precise conditions and the reasoning behind each.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two fatwa sources
Locate the opinions of al-Hinduwani (from al-Tabyin) and al-Munya. Al-Hinduwani sets a condition; al-Munya gives an absolute ruling for wife/mahram.
Al-Hinduwani is a later Hanafi jurist; al-Munya is another fatwa collection.
2
State each position clearly
Al-Hinduwani: killing is permissible only if shouting and non-lethal force will not deter the offender. Al-Munya: for wife or mahram, killing is permissible absolutely, regardless of deterrence.
3
Note the apparent contradiction
At first glance, the two opinions seem contradictory: one conditions, the other does not.
4
Follow the commentator's reconciliation
The commentator (author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) distinguishes the subject: al-Hinduwani's ruling applies to an unrelated woman (ajnabiyyah); al-Munya's applies to a wife or mahram.
The key phrase: 'فقد أفاد الفرق بين الأجنبية والزوجة والمحرم'.
5
Apply the reconciled ruling
For ajnabiyyah: condition required (inability to deter by less than killing). For wife/mahram: killing permissible immediately without condition.
This is the mufta bihi (operative) position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في التبيين وسئل الهندواني عن رجل وجد رجلاً مع امرأة أيحل له قتله؟ قال: إن كان يعلم أنه ينزجر بالصياح والضرب بما دون السلاح ،لا، وإن كان يعلم أنه لا ينزجر إلا بالقتل حل له القتل وإن طاوعته المرأة حل له قتلها أيضاً. وفي المنية : رأى رجلاً مع امرأته وهو يزني بها أو مع محرمه وهما مطاوعتان قتل الرجل والمرأة جميعاً .اهـ. فقد أفاد الفرق بين الأجنبية والزوجة والمحرم ففي الأجنبية لا يحل القتل إلا بالشرط المذكور من عدم الانزجار بالصياح والضرب، وفي غيرها يحل مطلقاً.
He said in al-Tabyin: Al-Hinduwani was asked about a man who found a man with a woman: is it permissible for him to kill him? He said: If he knows that he will be deterred by shouting and hitting with something less than a weapon, no; and if he knows that he will not be deterred except by killing, then killing him is permissible, and if the woman consented, then killing her is also permissible. And in al-Munya: He saw a man with his wife committing zina with her, or with his mahram, and both are consenting, then both the man and the woman are killed. End. So he derived the difference between an unrelated woman, a wife, and a mahram: for the unrelated woman, killing is not permissible except with the mentioned condition of not being deterred by shouting and hitting; for others, it is permissible absolutely.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage presents a fatawa-style ruling from classical Hanafi scholars on the permissibility of killing a person caught in the act of zina. The first opinion from al-Hinduwani sets a condition: if the offender can be deterred by shouting or non-lethal force, killing is not allowed; only if he refuses to desist and lethality is the only way to stop the sin, then killing the man (and the woman if she consented) is permissible. The second opinion from al-Munya (probably al-Munya al-Mufti or al-Munyat al-Mufti) seems to allow killing absolutely when the woman is the finder's wife or mahram. The commentator (likely the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) then synthesizes: the condition applies only to an unrelated woman (ajnabiyyah); for a wife or mahram, the killing is allowed unconditionally. This distinction is based on the stronger right of protection a man has over his wife and mahram. Note that this is a discretionary (ta'zir) matter, not a fixed hadd; the permissibility is contingent on necessity and the absence of alternative deterrence.

Key Terms
التعزير (al-ta'zir): Discretionary punishment left to judge's discretion; here it refers to killing as a ta'zir measure.
زنى (zina): Unlawful sexual intercourse; here the act being committed.
صياح (sayyah): Shouting loudly to deter the offender.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the reconciled view in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, when is it permissible to kill an unrelated woman (ajnabiyyah) found committing zina?
A) Only if the woman is married
B) Only if the man knows she cannot be deterred by shouting or non-lethal force
C) Always permissible under any circumstances
D) Only with permission of the judge

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of killing a found adulterer in the Hanafi school depends on the relationship and necessity; for an unrelated woman, killing is only allowed if lesser force cannot deter.

Conditions for Killing a Person Caught in Zina
Explains conditions for killing seen committing zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for killing someone caught in zina, distinguishing between the unrelated woman and one's wife or mahram.

Core Idea
Killing is only permissible for an unrelated woman if the culprit persists after warning; for wife/mahram, it is always permissible.

In this lesson, we examine an exception to the general prohibition of killing. The Hanafi school permits killing someone caught in zina only under strict conditions, and the ruling differs depending on the relationship of the woman involved. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the principle of forbidding evil (nahy an al-munkar) correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and legal context
The passage deals with killing a person seen committing zina. This is not a hadd punishment but an act of preventing evil (nahy an al-munkar). The permissibility is conditional.
This is distinct from the hadd penalty for zina which requires four witnesses.
2
Distinguish between cases
The passage differentiates between zina with an unrelated woman (ajnabiyya) and zina with one's wife or a mahram. For the latter, killing is permissible absolutely; for the former, only if the person does not desist after shouting and hitting.
Mahram refers to a woman marriage to whom is permanently prohibited (e.g., mother, sister).
3
Apply the condition for ajnabiyya
The condition is that the culprit must be warned (shouted at) and physically struck, yet he continues. Only then is killing permissible. The purpose is to stop the evil, not to punish after the fact.
If he desists, killing is not allowed.
4
Understand the underlying principle
Al-Mujtaba states the principle: anyone who sees another committing zina may kill him, but he refrains for fear of being killed and not believed. This shows the permissibility is based on the witness's fear of losing his life or credibility if the culprit resists.
The principle is not absolute; it is restricted by the condition mentioned for the unrelated woman.
5
Note the qiyas extension
The same principle is extended by analogy (qiyas) to oppressors, highway robbers, tax collectors, and all who persist in major sins. The illa is that they commit a great evil and do not desist despite warning.
The qiyas is jali (clear) because the underlying cause is shared.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود/ باب حد القذف
الأجنبية والزوجة والمحرم ففي الأجنبية لا يحل القتل إلا بالشرط المذكور من عدم الانزجار بالصياح والضرب، وفي غيرها يحل مطلقاً. وفي المجتبى الأصل في كل شخص إذا رأى يزني أن يحل له قتله وإنما يمتنع خوفاً أن يقتله ولا يصدق في أنه زنى. وعلى هذا القياس المكابرة بالظلم وقطاع الطريق وصاحب المكس وجميع الظلمة بأدنى شيء له قيمة وجميع الكبائر والأعونة والظلمة والسعاة فيباح قتل الكل ويثاب قاتلهم اهـ. ولم يذكر المصنف من يقيمه قالوا لكل مسلم إقامته حال مباشرة المعصية، وأما بعد الفراغ منها فليس ذلك لغير الحاكم. قال في القنية : رأى غيره على فاحشة موجبة للتعزير فعزره بغير إذن المحتسب فللمحتسب أن يعزر المعزز إن عزره بعد الفراغ منها . قال رضي الله عنه : قوله «إن عزره بعد الفراغ منها فيه إشارة إلى أنه لو عزره حال كونه مشغولاً بالفاحشة فله ذلك وأنه حسن لأن عن المنكر وكل واحد مأمور به وبعد الفراغ ليس بنهي عن المنكر لأن النهي عما مضى نهي لا يتصور فيتمحض تعزيراً وذلك إلى الإمام ا.هـ. وذكر قبله من عليه التعزير إذا قال لرجل أقم على التعزير ففعل ثم رفع إلى القاضي فإن القاضي يحتسب بذلك التعزير الذي أقامه بنفسه ا هـ . وفي المجتبى : فأما إقامة التعزير فقيل لصاحب الحق كالقصاص، وقيل للإمام لأن صاحب الحق قد يسرف فيه غلظاً بخلاف القصاص لأنه مقدر بخلاف التعزير الواجب حقاً الله تعالى حيث يتولى إقامته كل أحد بحكم النيابة عن الله تعالى اهـ. وفي القنية : ضرب غيره بغير حق وضربه المضروب أيضاً أنهما يعزران بإقامة التعزير بالبادي منهما لأنه أظلم والوجوب عليه أسبق اهـ. الهندواني ويجوز يقال نكر المرأة دلالة على أنه لا فرق بين الزوجة والأجنبية، وقد أفصح عن ذلك في الخانية حيث قال : رأى رجلاً يزني بامرأته أو بامرأة رجل آخر وهو محصن فصاح به ولم يهرب ولم يمتنع عن الزنا حل لهذا الرجل قتله، وإن قتله فلا قصاص عليه. وذكر مثله في السرقة حيث قال : رأى رجلاً يسرق ماله فصاح به أو ينقب حائطه أو حائط غيره وهو معروف بالسرقة فصاح به ولم يهرب حل قتله ولا قصاص عليه .اهـ. وغاية الأمر أن ما في منية المفتي وعليه جرى الخبازي في مختصر المحيط مطلقاً لكن يجب حمله على التقييد توفيقاً بين كلامهم. ومن هنا جزم ابن وهبان في نظمه بالشرط المذكور مطلقاً وهو الحق واعلم أنه في الخانية شرط في جواز قتل الزاني أن يكون محصناً وفي السارق أن يكون معروفاً بالسرقة وبالأول جزم الطرسوسي، ورده ابن وهبان بأنه ليس الحد بل من الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر وهو حسن فإن هذا المنكر حيث تعين القتل طريقاً في إزالته فلا معنى لاشتراط الإحصان فيه ولذا أطلقه البزازي. قوله : (وذكر قبله الخ) قال في النهر : هذا محمول في حق العبد على أنهما حكماه ففي فتح القدير الذي يجب حقاً للعبد لتوفقه على الدعوى لا يقيمه إلا الحاكم إلا أن يحكما فيه قوله : ( وفي القنية ضرب غيره بغير حق الخ) قال الرملي : قدم أنهما إذا تشاتما تكافأ إذا لم يكن بين يدي القاضي فراجعه في شرح قوله «ولو قال يا زاني محصناً»
Book of Hudud / Chapter of Qadhf: Regarding the unrelated woman, the wife, and the mahram: for the unrelated woman, killing is not permissible except with the mentioned condition of not being deterred by shouting and hitting; for others, it is permissible absolutely. In al-Mujtaba, the principle is that for any person who sees someone committing zina, it is permissible for him to kill him; he only refrains out of fear that he might be killed and not believed that he committed zina. By this analogy, the one who oppresses with injustice, highway robbers, the tax collector, and all oppressors for the least thing of value, and all major sins, helpers, oppressors, and agents are included; killing all of them is permitted and their killer is rewarded. End. The author did not mention who administers it; they said: every Muslim administers it at the time of direct commission of sin; but after completion, that is not for other than the ruler. He said in al-Qunyah: He saw another committing an indecency that necessitates ta'zir, and he gave ta'zir without the permission of the muhtasib; then the muhtasib may give ta'zir to the one who gave ta'zir if he gave ta'zir after completion. The author said: His statement 'if he gave ta'zir after completion' indicates that if he gave ta'zir while he was engaged in the indecency, he has that right, and it is good, because forbidding evil is commanded of everyone; after completion, it is not forbidding evil because forbidding what has passed is not conceivable, so it is purely ta'zir, and that is for the imam. End. And before that, he mentioned: The one upon whom ta'zir is due, if he said to a man 'Administer ta'zir on me' and he did it, then he raised it to the judge, the judge counts that ta'zir that he administered himself. End. And in al-Mujtaba: As for administering ta'zir, it was said it is for the owner of the right like qisas, and it was said it is for the imam because the owner of the right might be excessive in severity, unlike qisas because it is fixed; unlike ta'zir which is obligatory as a right of Allah, where everyone administers it by deputyship from Allah. End. And in al-Qunyah: One struck another without right, and the struck one also struck him; both are given ta'zir, starting with the initiator because he is more unjust and the obligation on him is prior. End. al-Hindawani: It is permissible; the indefinite form of 'woman' indicates that there is no difference between the wife and an unrelated woman. And this is clarified in al-Khaniyya where he said: He saw a man committing zina with his wife or with another man's wife, and he is muhsin; he shouted at him and he did not flee nor desist from zina; it is permissible for this man to kill him, and if he kills him, there is no qisas upon him. And he mentioned similarly in theft: He saw a man stealing his property, he shouted at him, or he was breaking into his wall or another's wall while being known for theft; he shouted at him and he did not flee; it is permissible to kill him and there is no qisas upon him. End. The upshot is that what is in Munyat al-Mufti and what al-Khabbazi followed in Mukhtasar al-Muhit is absolute, but it must be restricted to reconcile their statements. Hence Ibn Wahban in his versification decisively stated the mentioned condition absolutely, and that is correct. Know that in al-Khaniyya, the condition for the permissibility of killing the zani is that he be muhsin, and for the thief that he be known for theft; al-Tarsusi decisively stated the first, but Ibn Wahban refuted him, saying it is not a hadd but from commanding good and forbidding evil, which is good; and since this evil is such that killing is determined as a means to remove it, there is no meaning to stipulating ihsan in it; thus al-Bazzazi made it absolute. His statement: (And before that he mentioned) said in al-Nahr: This is interpreted concerning the slave that they both judged; in Fath al-Qadir, that which is obligatory as a right of the slave based on his claim is not administered except by the ruler, unless they both judge in it. His statement: (And in al-Qunyah: one struck another without right...) al-Ramli said: He stated that if they insult each other, they are equal if not before the judge; so refer to his commentary on his statement: 'If he said, O zani, muhsin.'
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the chapter of qadhf, specifically addressing when killing a person caught in the act of zina or theft is permissible. The author distinguishes between an unrelated woman (ajnabiyya) and one's wife or mahram: for the former, killing is only allowed if the person does not desist after shouting and hitting; for the latter, it is allowed absolutely. The text then cites al-Mujtaba to establish the general principle that anyone who sees another committing zina may kill him, but he refrains for fear of not being believed. This principle is extended by qiyas (analogy) to oppressors, highway robbers, tax collectors, and all tyrants. A key point is the timing of ta'zir: during the commission of the sin, any Muslim may administer ta'zir (since it is part of forbidding evil), but after the act, only the ruler (imam) may do so. The passage also discusses who should administer ta'zir—whether the victim (like qisas) or the imam—and notes that striking without right leads to ta'zir for both parties, with the initiator being punished first. The text then delves into conditions for killing: some scholars require the adulterer to be muhsin (married) and the thief to be known for theft, while others (like Ibn Wahban) reject these conditions, arguing that this is not a hadd but rather a means of forbidding evil. The passage concludes with a note on the interpretation of rulings concerning slaves and mutual insults.

Key Terms
أجنبية (ajnabiyya): A woman who is not a wife or mahram; a non-mahram woman.
محرم (mahram): A woman to whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to blood, marriage, or suckling.
صياح (ṣiyāḥ): Shouting; verbal warning to stop the act.
ضرب (ḍarb): Hitting or striking physically.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it permissible to kill someone seen committing zina with an unrelated woman?
A) At any time, regardless of their response
B) Only if the person does not desist after being shouted at and hit
C) Only if the person is a married adulterer (muhsin)
D) Only if the killing is authorized by the imam

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits killing someone caught in zina with an unrelated woman only if the culprit persists after a verbal and physical warning.

Timing and Authority for Administering Ta'zir
Explains timing and authority for ta'zir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between administering ta'zir during the commission of a sin (permitted for any Muslim) and after the act (reserved for the imam), and state who can administer ta'zir in both cases.

Core Idea
Ta'zir during the sin is part of forbidding evil; after the sin, it is punishment and only for the ruler.

This lesson examines the procedural rules for ta'zir (discretionary punishment). The timing of ta'zir is crucial: during the act, any Muslim may administer it as part of commanding good and forbidding evil; after the act, it becomes a punitive measure that only the imam (ruler) can carry out. We also explore who should administer ta'zir in cases of personal rights versus rights of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act: ta'zir for indecency
The passage discusses ta'zir for acts that are not subject to fixed hadd penalties. The specific case is a person seen committing an indecency (fahisha) that requires ta'zir.
Ta'zir is left to the judge's discretion.
2
Distinguish timing: during vs after the act
The passage states that every Muslim may administer ta'zir at the time of direct commission of the sin (hala mubasharat al-ma'siya). After the act ('adam al-faragh minha), only the imam (or his deputy) can do so.
The muhtasib (market inspector) may ta'zir the person who gave ta'zir after completion.
3
Understand the rationale
During the act, ta'zir is part of forbidding evil (nahy an al-munkar), which is obligatory on every Muslim. After the act, forbidding what is past is not conceivable, so it becomes pure punishment (ta'zir mahd), which is the prerogative of the imam.
The author says: 'after completion, it is not forbidding evil because forbidding what has passed is not conceivable.'
4
Examine the authority for ta'zir
Two views are cited: one says ta'zir is for the owner of the right (like qisas), because the harm is personal; the other says it is for the imam, because the owner might be excessive. The passage notes that ta'zir for the right of Allah is administered by anyone by deputyship from Allah.
For Allah's rights, everyone is a deputy; for personal rights, it is like qisas and requires the ruler or the victim's control.
5
Apply to mutual striking case
The passage gives an example: if one person strikes another without right and the victim retaliates, both are given ta'zir, but the initiator is punished first because he is more unjust.
This shows the principle of starting with the aggressor.

Source Text

يقتله ولا يصدق في أنه زنى. وعلى هذا القياس المكابرة بالظلم وقطاع الطريق وصاحب المكس وجميع الظلمة بأدنى شيء له قيمة وجميع الكبائر والأعونة والظلمة والسعاة فيباح قتل الكل ويثاب قاتلهم اهـ. ولم يذكر
